Pan Gongzhan and Tang Demin Request the Establishment of a National Art Museum

One of the Proposals to the First Congress

Pan Gongzhan and Tang Demin believe that the impact of art's social education on national fortune is great, so they specifically proposed to the Municipal Congress that the Central Ministry of Interior and Ministry of Education jointly establish a National Art Museum to promote the realization of the Three Principles of the People. The original text is as follows: (A) Reasons: The prosperity and decline of a country and nation are greatly related to school education, but even more so to social education. The accuracy of the national spirit's transmission, the improvement of social order, and the enhancement of national wisdom can all be measured by the degree of development of social education. Half of the function of social education is related to art. Although art is not as necessary as food, clothing, housing, and transportation in life, it is of great value in increasing the meaning of human life. Film, drama, music, and painting are all closely related to life, directly shaping emotions and harmonizing life. Indirectly, they can cause various good and evil responses in the human heart, and cultivate creative desires. The so-called joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness are not just emotional impulses in a short time, but contain the active meaning of controlling life. This is undeniable. In terms of quantity (the mimeograph is blurred here), the efficiency of art's control cannot be ignored. Taking only the film industry in Shanghai as an example, at least 100,000 people receive the direct intuition of film (calculated with 40 cinemas, each with 2,500 people). Drama is half of that. Taking this as an example for China, more than ten million people are dominated by film and drama every day. The eye-catching nature of painting is even more widespread, and the lyrics and scores of music can spread even further. This is the two-dimensional effectiveness of art, which no one can deny. However, if we silently observe the currently popular films, dramas, music, and paintings, what is the impact on the nation? Most of the films are imported. The domestic films are biased towards gods and monsters. There are few that are beneficial to the welfare of our nation and society, like stars in the morning. Most of the dramas, especially Peking Opera, are based on unofficial history, which is not superstitious but biased towards feudal thoughts. It has long lost its value in the current era. New dramas are still in their infancy, and it is rare to find those that are suitable for our ideals and benefit the prosperity of the country and nation. The same applies to music and painting. Our country is in a period of transition. In order to make the people understand the Three Principles of the People, accept Sun Yat-sen's teachings, and subtly increase the people's sense of meaning and responsibility towards the country and nation, as well as arouse the people's interest in construction, in addition to seeking help from schools, it is necessary to double the results with less effort.

Page 14

To be effective, suitable for all ages, both men and women, there is no way other than to focus on the social education of art. Art is the most effective weapon for propaganda and has long been recognized by the general public. However, to achieve this great wish by seeking help from commercial art institutions or groups is like climbing a tree to catch fish. Although the government's Ministry of Interior and Ministry of Education have organized a censorship committee to ban all films that are harmful to the welfare of our nation, the meaning of this only extends to passive prevention and reducing the evils of films, dramas, music, and paintings on the nation. To actively seek results from the social education of art, only the state can promote it. Methods: (1) The congress should petition the central government to instruct the Ministry of Interior and Ministry of Education to jointly establish a National Art Museum. The National Art Museum should have four departments: film, drama, music, and painting. Each department should establish a committee and appoint specialized personnel to serve as members. The collection and editing of all film, drama, music, and painting materials should be centered on enlightening the Three Principles of the People, especially paying attention to inspiring national significance, arousing the people's sense of national responsibility, and interests in construction, and promoting the inherent morality of loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, faith, righteousness, and peace. In addition to promoting the produced films in cinemas at home and abroad, the Film Department should establish national cinemas in the capital and Shanghai, Beijing, Guangzhou, Hankou, Tianjin, and the provincial capitals of various provinces. The Drama Department should divide into old and new dramas. Although old dramas have lost their value in the current era, they still have a deep influence in society and cannot be banned. The only way is to improve their scripts and lyrics. In addition to printing and distributing the improved scripts and lyrics to various old-style theaters and directors, national theaters should also be established in the capital, Shanghai, Hankou, Beijing, Tianjin, Guangzhou, and the provincial capitals of various provinces. In addition to printing and selling the scripts of new dramas for local drama clubs and students to purchase, national new drama theaters should also be established in the capital, Shanghai, Hankou, Beijing, Tianjin, and the provincial capitals of various provinces. In addition to compiling Chinese and Western music scores for schools and various musical groups to purchase, the Music Department should also establish music academies in various prosperous cities. In addition to promoting works with the Three Principles of the People as the central theme, the Painting Department should hold painting exhibitions every year in the capital and various prosperous cities, and reward those with excellent achievements. Then the atmosphere will change and the results will be predictable. As for the expenses of the National Art Museum, the Ministry of Interior and Ministry of Education should prepare a budget and submit it to the National Government for allocation.

Various Labor Unions to Propose Motions at the Municipal Assembly

The Municipal Assembly of this city is scheduled to open on July 1st. Dozens of labor unions, including the Municipal Postal and Publishing Unions, considering the urgent need to expedite the implementation of various resolutions regarding labor movements passed by the National Assembly, have specially prepared a motion to be submitted for discussion at the opening of the assembly. Simultaneously, they will dispatch representatives to request permission to attend the assembly as observers to present their case in person. It is reported that the official submission and motion have already been drafted. The following is a transcription:

Submitting this document to request the dispatch of representatives and respectfully present the motion, requesting the Assembly to grant permission for attendance as observers and to present the motion for discussion, so that it may be publicly resolved and implemented.

We respectfully note that the National Assembly has resolved three items regarding the reform of labor movement organization laws, which have been submitted to the National Government for consideration and handling. First, the revision of the Labor Union Law and the Factory Law to protect the interests of workers. Second, the establishment of national, provincial, municipal, and county-level federations of labor unions. Third, the promulgation of special labor union laws. The Assembly resolved two items regarding the guarantee and relief of workers' livelihoods, which have been submitted to the National Government for consideration and handling. These are the diligent implementation of labor education and the relief of unemployed workers. All the plans formulated and resolved by the National Assembly in accordance with the Party's political program and in compliance with Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings are the unanimous demands of workers nationwide and the guiding principles for the Party and the government to actively rectify the labor movement during the period of political tutelage. We respectfully submit this.

Attached is the motion on the left (Original text of the motion):

We earnestly request that this be forwarded to the Central Government, consulting with the National Government to quickly guide the resolutions on the labor movement from the National Assembly, thoroughly revise the Labor Union Law and the Factory Law, and add articles to the Labor Union Law to organize national, provincial, municipal, and county-level federations of labor unions, promulgate special labor union laws, and diligently implement labor education and relief for unemployed workers. Is this appropriate? We respectfully await a public resolution.

(Reasons)

This city is the center of the national labor movement. The labor movement in this city is where our Party's revolutionary strength lies. Therefore, rectifying the labor movement in this city directly serves the interests of workers and indirectly contributes to the development of a new life for our Party. This session of the Assembly coincides with the opening more than a month after the closing of the National Assembly. It bears a significant mission and arduous responsibility for supervising and promoting the implementation of the resolutions of the National Assembly. Whether the several major resolutions concerning the labor movement are implemented or not has a particularly significant impact on the labor movement in this city. Therefore, this motion is put forward with great seriousness.

(Measures)

We respectfully request that the Assembly resolve to promptly forward this to the Central Government, consulting with the National Government to implement this as soon as possible. Submitted by: Shanghai Publishing Industry Labor Union, Postal Labor Union, Textile Industry Labor Union of the Seventh District, Water and Electricity Industry Labor Union of the Sixth District, Water and Electricity Industry Labor Union of the First District, etc.

Ministry of Industry and Ministry of Finance Telegraph to Urge Fundamental Solution for Silk Industry Public Bonds Distribution Method

Experts have already drafted concrete methods

Executive Committee discussed yesterday and deemed further study necessary

The Fourth Executive Committee of the Jiang-Zhe Silk Industry Public Bonds held a discussion yesterday at the Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry. The attendees were committee members Mu Ouchu, Chu Huiseng, Shen [name missing]chen, Deng Bingwen, Qian Fenghao, Lu Shutang, silk industry experts Zheng Bijang, Zhou Tingding, Ge Jingzhong, and Cheng Zhenjun, Director of the Industrial Department of the Ministry of Industry, ten people in total, with Mu Ouchu as chairman. The discussion details, fundamental solution proposals, and the telegraphs from the two ministries are recorded below.

Discussion Details:

The discussion yesterday focused on the fundamental problems of the silk industry. First, experts presented draft plans for improving machinery and improving sericulture. Then the discussion began. However, when discussing the issue of receiving subsidies for purchasing and adding cocoon boiling machines in the machinery improvement section, the discussion reached a standstill due to the stipulation that the machinery could not be resold after being equipped with cocoon boiling machines. The question was, to whom would the ownership of the machinery belong in the future: the silk manufacturers, the landlords, or would another method be devised? After a lengthy discussion, it was generally agreed that this issue was very important. It was resolved to wait for each association to conduct a detailed study and then discuss it again on Saturday (July 4th). As for the Ministry of Finance and Ministry of Industry's urgent telegraph to submit the entire distribution plan to the ministry for review by July 2nd, it was resolved to request an extension due to insufficient time.

Telegraphs from the Two Ministries:

The Ministry of Industry and Ministry of Finance telegraphed to urge the distribution plan, stating: (Official salutations omitted) We received your telegram. Upon reviewing Article 3 of the amended Jiang-Zhe Silk Industry Public Bonds Regulations, it stipulates that the use of the silk industry public bonds is divided into fundamental and superficial items. Now is the period for proceeding with the distribution. It is appropriate to advance both the fundamental and superficial points at the same time. According to your telegram, the Third Meeting of the Association resolved to distribute the four million yuan for superficial items first. As for the fundamental one, a concrete method has not yet been discussed. The Association should quickly draft a detailed plan for the fundamental method and submit it to the ministry for review as necessary. As for the superficial method, although the Association resolved to consider two silk reeling machines and one bale of silk as a unit, the current detailed situation of each factory in Jiang-Zhe should be thoroughly investigated as the standard for the distribution of public bonds. The person in charge should be responsible for creating a detailed table, including (1) the factory name, (2) the address, (3) the number of machines, (4) whether self-owned or leased, (5) the number of silk bales, (6) the amount of bond notes that should be received, and (7) the seal of the person in charge, and submit it to the ministry for review within ten days of receiving this document. Await further instructions. Seal of the Ministry of Finance and Ministry of Industry.

The First District Branch of the Citizens' Association Strives for Rental Housing Rights

The First District Branch of the Shanghai Special District Citizens' Federation sent a letter to the Citizens' Federation yesterday, proposing the motion that citizens should have the right to rental housing.

Respected Sirs, the original text reads, "In order to propose that citizens should have the right to rental housing, we request that your association expand the movement to achieve its goals, so as to secure a peaceful residence and benefit commercial transportation."

We note that renting houses for residence, whether in commercial ports or inland, has always been customary and without much conflict. However, in Shanghai's concessions in recent years, with the increase in commerce and population, the prices of real estate and rents have not only increased due to natural trends, but also because the Municipal Council has forcibly estimated high price standards in order to increase its donation revenue, which has promoted their rapid increase. As a result, those who operate real estate have greatly benefited, not only increasing their rental value at any time, but also setting out huge amounts of tips, digging fees, opening fees and other names to satisfy their greed, and the shop residents who pay the stars have greatly suffered their fruits. The capital fee for merchants to set up shops is already half of the rental price, not to mention the cost of decoration and property. And those who have slow business, one month's profit, or not enough to pay one month's rent. However, this situation is unique to a few and can be ignored. The most recently discovered situation is that tenants are unable to enjoy the happiness of living and working in peace and are living in anxiety, which is the evil practice of landlords arbitrarily increasing rents and forcing evictions.

For example, (A) the originally set rent is already expensive, and the tenant does not owe any rent, but the landlord takes the initiative to increase the price, and the percentage increase is extremely large, so that the tenant cannot afford it. They can also negotiate a reduction, but the evil ones have no accommodation at all, otherwise they order a forced eviction. (B) The age of the house may not have reached the time of demolition in fact, the landlord wants to renovate to increase the rent, that is, arbitrarily force the eviction. After the new house is completed, the monthly rent will be doubled compared to before, and the cost of renovation will be borrowed from the tip. Every time the original tenant is unable to continue renting the house, if a third person digs for rent, the landlord will covet the heavy profit and cleverly set up various plans to make them move out, regardless of the law and human feelings, so that the original tenant is forced to stop business, not only the shop owner is damaged, but also the employees who depend on the owner for their livelihood are unemployed. (D) Large capitalists who trust the doctrine of the company, determine the large area of land, rent land from the owner to build houses, or for real estate profits, become the owner of the company. The owner also covets its profits and disregards everything, willing to sacrifice hundreds of tenants for one tenant. (E) Tenants and landlords have disputes, often the landlord based on the magic of money, the hand of lightning speed, or use of separation tricks, or use of oppressive behavior, cutting off water and electricity, hitting the wall to dismantle the house, nothing can not be done.

The above five points are only the main points. Although it is not a fact that happens from time to time, the fact of the matter has happened a lot, and it is also verified.

In short, its harm also has five points, one is to destroy the rental habit, the second is to infringe on the legal rights of renting, the third is to hinder public order, the fourth is to disturb social stability, and the fifth is to lose morality. If this goes on, the merchants and residents who rent houses among the citizens will be like hawkers who bear the burden, not as good as hawkers. Those who set up stalls and bear the burden, originally those who seek to provide, may as well seek profit from the east and west. Stores must have a fixed address, often moving, new drafts are difficult to find, that is, to get land, business is damaged, decoration and property advertising rent, etc., must be to the customers who need electricity, do not lose more than half. As for the household, there are also various disadvantages, the area of the association, located in the center of the concession, see and hear the most, and the citizens in this area are also deeply harmed. If we do not find a way to rescue them as soon as possible, it will inevitably affect the imperial industry and the whole city, and even affect the inland, its harm is not known. If we talk about rescue measures, the most positive way is to petition the National Government and the municipal government to issue special laws and regulations on the protection of residence rights, and the citizens' organization has a systematic and united specialized committee to agree on limiting the profit-making degree of landlords, or dividing the concessions into sections, depending on the prosperity of the location, the newness of the old houses, to set the rental price standard, regulate a rental rules, to the authorities for the record, requiring the landlord to recognize and accept. The passive way is to have a group of tenants in the city deal with it appropriately according to the severity of the case. However, this matter is a big deal, and it is not possible to gather the sympathy of the tenants and citizens of the city and give it a big movement. Therefore, after the executive committee, according to the public opinion of the majority of members of the association's inaugural meeting, the meeting resolved to ask your association to discuss, gather together, and seek permanent peace and happiness.

Zhengji Company Will Move to Qingdao

Seeking to Break Free from Japanese Shackles

Requesting Central Government Subsidy

Dismissing Japanese Employees:

Among Chinese commercial shipping companies, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is the giant in the South, while Zhengji Company is the largest in North China. Due to devastation by warlords, it moved its headquarters to Dalian Bay. Over the years, it has suffered oppression from the Japanese and has felt considerable pain. The various taxes paid to the Japanese each year are also quite substantial. Among the more than twenty commercial vessels, many of the senior crew members were also Japanese. In recent years, in order to recover outward flowing interests, it first dismissed more than twenty Japanese crew members from each vessel and replaced them with domestic shipping professionals. The company intends to replace all of its Japanese employees with Chinese citizens in succession.

Moving the Headquarters:

Mr. Zhang Benzheng, the person in charge of the company, feels that the shipping industry has been depressed in recent years and has also been subjected to various restrictions by the Japanese. He is determined to break free from the Japanese shackles. When the company expanded in the year of Yichou, the Northeast Party authorities joined as government shareholders. Now, Mr. Zhang has informed the Liaoning authorities that he has decided to close the Dalian Bay headquarters and move the headquarters to Qingdao, which is under Chinese jurisdiction. This has been agreed upon and is already in the planning stage. Once the Qingdao headquarters location is prepared, the relocation will take place immediately.

Requesting a Subsidy:

Currently, the shipping industry is in a downturn. Mr. Zhang Benzheng, the person in charge of the company, has petitioned the Central Government for an appropriate subsidy to enable the development of Chinese commercial vessels in North China. It is said that Mr. Zhang intends to go to the capital in person to present the current state of business to the Ministry of Transportation in order to achieve the goal of government subsidy.

Orders Jianghai Customs Not to Issue Passports

The Ministry of Transportation recently learned that the British Taikoo Company's New Beijing steamship has been sailing from Shanghai to Putuo without permission from the Chinese authorities, which infringes on China's territorial waters. Therefore, it has specifically notified Jianghai Customs to ban it. It is learned that after receiving the notification, Jianghai Customs, in addition to formally negotiating with Taikoo Company, will not issue navigation passports.

Department Store Industry Firmly Requests Reduction of Business Tax

The Shanghai Department Store Industry Association believes that the business tax rate of three per mille is truly unbearable and violates the previously promulgated ministerial guidelines and the resolutions of the National Conference on the Abolition of Likin, disregarding the months of correspondence and urgent appeals from merchants and citizens. They are shocked and beyond words. Therefore, they convened an emergency meeting yesterday and resolved that the items sold by department stores are all daily necessities for ordinary people or belong to the scope that should be promoted. Business has been difficult in recent years, and they have long been in a state of being outwardly strong but inwardly weak. If they are taxed at a high rate that violates the guidelines, they will have no choice but to comply with the notice issued by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Tax Research Committee on February 28th: 1. If the business tax in any province or city exceeds the regulations of the Executive Yuan, there is no basis for collection by the provincial and municipal governments. 2. Merchants and citizens in various industries should not disobey the order to pay the original tax and should wait for a solution. Representatives will be elected to present the unavoidable difficulties to the Tax Research Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and actively request a reduction, to a maximum of no more than two per mille.

Chinese Medicine Association Willing to Fulfill Obligations to the Poor and Sick

Reply to Municipal Health Bureau Letter

The Shanghai Municipal Government approved the Shanghai Party Department's request to instruct the Health Bureau to notify Chinese and Western doctors in the city to fulfill their obligations to the poor and sick, so as to value the lives of citizens. The Chinese Medicine Association replied to the Bureau yesterday, saying: "In reply, we have received your letter, which states that the Shanghai Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang has written to the effect that the Sixth District Party Department of the Association has submitted a document stating that registered doctors in the city should fulfill their obligations to the poor and that the Municipal Health Bureau should be consulted and ordered to comply. Accordingly, it has been found that the city has a large population, and the majority are coolies and the poor. They usually struggle to make ends meet. Once they are sick, they moan and fall, and there is no one to turn to. It is often heard and seen that one person is sick and the whole family is waiting to die. This is especially true in summer and autumn. Therefore, it is appropriate to widely establish clinics to benefit the poor and sick. Moreover, helping the sick and rescuing disasters and treating diseases are all stipulated in the Party's political program. Shanghai should take the lead in implementing this. The Standing Committee of the Association has resolved to amend this and forward it to the Municipal Government for the record. Accordingly, we enclose a copy of the letter for your reference. We hope you will verify this and give us a reply. The doctors originally had a compassionate heart and should give appropriate treatment to the poor. In addition to issuing a separate order, this letter is to be forwarded to you. We hope you will forward this to the doctors so that they can practice it in moderation, so as to benefit the poor and comply with good intentions. In view of the foregoing, we have found that Chinese medicine has always been compassionate in treating diseases. There is a precedent for not counting the poor. In order to take care of the health of the people, our association has established a Chinese Hospital to meet the needs of society. The Bureau of Society has already filed a record. Other Chinese medicine clinics, such as Renji Hall, Guangyi Chinese Hospital, Qianyi Traumatology Hospital, Hubian Guangyi Chinese Hospital, Guangyi Shantang, Hunan Shenzhou Hospital, Fuli Hospital, Boji Benevolent Society, Guangren Shantang, Zhisheng Benevolent Institute, Weizhong Benevolent Hall, Yishan Society, Lianyi Benevolent Association, Yuanji Benevolent Hall, Cantonese Merchants Hospital, Chinese Hospital, Hualong Chinese Hospital, Chaozhou Heji Hospital, Siming Hospital, etc., either provide treatment and medicine or provide wards for treatment. As for the society, it feels that it has done a little bit of its duty. Because of the letter, in addition to notifying the members, we now enclose a list of the locations, times, and methods of Chinese medicine clinics in this city for your reference. We hope that you will publish this in the newspaper to benefit the people, which is no small matter. We reply to the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau.

A Brief History of the Shanghai Concessions, compiled by Mr. Cen Dechang, has recently been published. It is divided into twenty-eight chapters, with approximately 100,000 words. It covers all the rare and interesting stories of the past eighty years, and it includes many valuable charts and diagrams. It is truly an essential book for people traveling to Shanghai. Candle Prices to Increase Again Today

The Shanghai Candle Industry Association has repeatedly received reports from members that the raw materials for candle making have recently been increasing rapidly. Based on the current candle prices, it is difficult to maintain even the cost. They requested a meeting to discuss raising prices. The Association convened a members' meeting the day before yesterday. A letter has already been sent to all members, notifying them to comply.

Female Youth Association's Tutorial Classes Close

The tutorial classes of the Female Youth Association are scheduled to hold a summer vacation closing ceremony at 4:00 PM on June 30th. Report cards will be distributed, and students from each grade will perform. There will be speeches, English dialogues, English storytelling, freehand exercises, etc. Members of the Association and family members of students are welcome to participate. The fall semester is scheduled to begin on September 3rd.

Trade Association News

Soybean and Rice Industry: The Soybean and Rice Industry Trade Association issued an urgent notice yesterday, stating, "To whom it may concern, our association, after a special meeting of all members from both the northern and southern markets, has resolved on the following procedures for remitting payments to rice dealers: (1) All payments from rice dealers to material suppliers must be remitted by the end of each month, whether long or short, according to the Gregorian calendar. A remittance book must be included to obtain a receipt from the supplier for verification. Payments without a receipt will not be considered valid. (2) Rice dealers remitting payments will be subsidized for transportation costs by the association at a rate of 50 copper coins per hundred yuan, with proportional increases for larger amounts. The above procedures will be implemented starting July 1st. In addition to sending a letter to the Rice Dealers Trade Association in this city to inform all rice dealers, please strictly implement this notice."

Shaoxing Wine Industry: The Shaoxing Wine Industry Association held its tenth executive and standing committee meeting yesterday, chaired by Ding Jinsheng, to discuss various matters: (1) The annual fee for the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for the 20th year of the Republic will be allocated from the association's monthly loss account. Any shortfall will be the responsibility of the chairman, to be drawn from the pledged funds. (2) The association is unable to subscribe to the Ministry of Finance's short-term treasury bonds for the 20th year of the Republic and has responded accordingly. (3) Regarding the new system of weights and measures, as the testing institute has not yet made preparations, it is proposed that the association entrust Comrade Sun Guangben to have a tinsmith come to the association within five days to estimate the price. Once an agreement is reached, the tinsmith will register with the testing institute to produce measures of one tael, two taels, four taels, half a catty, and four catties, calculated according to the new standard. (5) Public matters are still under consideration. (6) Regarding the increase in transportation costs in Zhabei, Xu Meisheng, representative of Tongda Chang, and Wang Liankui, representative of Lian Tai, were present to discuss and moderately increase the rates to alleviate the burden on members. The two representatives signed off after verification. (7) The association's land deed will be taken from under the inscription and submitted to the Land Bureau for a new deed.

Coal and Stone Barge Industry: The Coal and Stone Barge Industry Trade Association held its inaugural meeting at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. Representatives from 39 firms, totaling 54 people, attended. Zhu Ya Kui from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Hu Yuqi from the Social Affairs Bureau, and Sun Mingqi from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce were present to provide guidance. Tang Jin, representative of the Xiejin Barge Transportation Company, was elected chairman. As a result of the election, Ruan Xuezun, Tang Jinshu, Yuan Genquan, Zhu Shishu, Yu Liyun, Fan Deyu, Hu Yinsheng, Xu Kairen, Zhang Caiyu, Wang Shiyou, Chen Xianqing, Cao Yuyu, Li Gaosong, Hu Xiangshi, and Zhu Xueqin were elected as executive committee members.

Dried Goods Industry: The Dried Goods Industry Trade Association held a meeting of members at the market in this city yesterday, chaired by Yu Jingyan. 1. Discussed Clause 10 of the General Regulations of the Association's Articles of Association, which states that for every ten additional employees, each company or firm should appoint one additional representative, but not exceeding three. Due to the long-standing nature of this regulation, very few store clerks have registered as representatives with the association, making it difficult for the association to proceed. It was resolved that a detailed explanation should be issued, informing store clerks that appointing representatives to the association is for the purpose of making them natural members, exempt from membership fees, and protecting their rights. The notice should instruct all stores to appoint representatives to register with the association according to the law. 2. Discussed how to raise donations for the Jiangxi disaster relief fund. It was resolved that members of the association should be encouraged to donate one month's salary. All members were notified to proceed accordingly before the meeting adjourned. Vegetable Industry: The Vegetable Industry Trade Association held an executive meeting yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. Executive committee members and over 30 members were present, chaired by Chen Shushen, the standing committee member. The chairman reported the purpose of the meeting and read out documents from various institutions. Discussed various matters: (1) Regarding the order to implement weights and measures, it was generally agreed that less than 50 businesses in this city currently use scales, and the stipulated municipal scale only has one weight, creating many obstacles in the procedure. It was resolved to request the authorities to make changes to facilitate matters. It was resolved that the association should purchase 50 municipal scales with a capacity of 20 to 150 catties each and distribute them to members for replacement. However, each scale should have an additional weight ranging from one to 29 catties, so that one scale can be used for both large and small quantities. The Social Affairs Bureau should be requested to approve an additional fee for ordering and issuing scales to facilitate procurement and use. (2) Regarding the vacancy left by Executive Committee member Chen Liansun, it was resolved that the vacancy left by Chen Liansun should be filled by the first alternate, Zhang Degui, according to the law. He was immediately sworn in. The Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau will be notified of the replacement for record-keeping. Finally, various matters regarding the association's affairs were discussed before the meeting adjourned.

Wax Industry: The Wax Industry Trade Association held an extraordinary joint executive meeting the day before yesterday, chaired by Fan Songsheng, who first reported on the meeting's circumstances. (A) Matters for discussion: (1) Whether or not to subscribe to public bonds. (2) Jiangxi disaster relief. (3) New weights and measures. (B) Resolutions: (1) Regarding the committee's request to subscribe to 1,000 yuan worth of bonds, as there are only eleven businesses in total and the industry's business is not good, it was decided to subscribe to a modest 200 yuan. The resolution was passed. (2) Each business should donate as much as possible for Jiangxi disaster relief. Passed. (3) The implementation of the new weights and measures system is imminent and the industry should be notified again. Resolved and passed. The standing committee of this association has resolved to allow orders to be placed with weights and measures manufacturers. All members must first report to the association the type and quantity of new equipment they need to order so that bulk orders can be placed. The deadline is urgent and cannot be extended. Local News: Two Foreign Communists

A suspicious man and woman

Belgian passports found to be forged

Approximately 600 pieces of communist evidence

A Western man named Nielands, and a Western woman named Maude (also known as Wanda Keisen), both around 37 years old, claimed to be husband and wife, but lived separately. Nielands resided in Room 4, Building 235, Sichuan Road, while Maude resided in Room 30, Building 49, Sichuan Road. Their actions were highly suspicious. The police authorities paid close attention and assigned Western Detective McGregor to secretly investigate for a long time. Recently, it was discovered that the two were indeed well-known communists. They were arrested one after the other on the morning of the 15th of this month, and many communist documents were found in their residences. According to Nielands' confession, he was of Belgian nationality and his wife was French. The police contacted the Belgian and French consulates for investigation. As the two had not registered with the consulates when they came to Shanghai, there was no way to verify their identities. Therefore, both the Belgian and French consulates denied that Nielands and his wife were their citizens. Nielands then led the detectives to 74 Xihua Garden Road, claiming it was their joint residence. After searching the premises, the detectives found two passports, stating that both were of Belgian nationality. The police sent them to the Belgian consulate again. The Belgian consul, with passport proof, could not refuse and issued a search warrant, which was handed over to the police to send detectives to 74 Xihua Garden Road again for a thorough search. Various kinds of communist evidence were found, totaling about 600 pieces, including those obtained previously. Subsequently, the Belgian consul considered the case to be of great importance and telegraphed the Belgian government for verification. The reply received the day before yesterday stated that the two were definitely not of Belgian nationality and their passports were forged. The Belgian consul ordered them to be sent back to the police station for detention. Last night, they were sent to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. Judge Du Fuyao held a court session and briefly questioned them. As evidence needed to be investigated, he ordered them to be detained separately pending further interrogation.

Wu Chunzhi, Owner of Huayang Restaurant on Fuyou Road, Stabbed to Death

Negotiations to terminate the contract had just concluded

When a short man named Xiao Wang suddenly committed the crime

Around 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon, Wu Chunzhi, the owner of Huayang Restaurant, a dim sum shop located east of Small World on Fuyou Road in the Nanshi area, opposite the 9th Team of the Shanghai South Security Corps, was suddenly stabbed to death by a well-known friend. The details are very complicated. The following is a detailed account of the incident:

The background of Chen Xiaomei: Chen Xiaomei, a woman from Pudong, is 19 years old. Although her appearance is only average, she is exceptionally lively and articulate. Her parents love her very much. Her father, named Xue Rong, used to run wood carving and foreign goods businesses. During its peak, he had as many as four stores in Shanghai. However, Chen's fortune was unlucky and the stores closed one after another, leading to a complete downfall. His wife, Zhou, and the whole family now live in Lan Ni Du, Pudong, seeking labor work to make a living. Xiaomei now works as a cigarette packer at the Fuxin Tobacco Company on Kangti Road in the French Concession. Every morning, she crosses the river to work at the factory, returning home as late as 2:00 AM the next morning.

One woman engaged twice: Several years ago, Xiaomei and her family once lived near Small World in Nanshi for about eight or nine years. At that time, Xiaomei was still young and learned handicrafts with her mother in a nearby foreign jade shop. Two years ago, her mother arranged for Xiaomei to be betrothed to a fellow villager and worker in the foreign jade shop, nicknamed Short Xiao Wang. At the time of the engagement, the Wang family paid 40 yuan as betrothal money. However, Wang soon lost his job and his personal life became difficult, let alone getting married. Xiaomei's mother changed her mind and remarried her to a man from Pudong named Zhou Heshang. They were married in January of last year according to the lunar calendar.

Negotiated solution: Seeing that he had lost both the woman and the money, Short Xiao Wang felt resentful and invited his friends Tang Gengquan and Chen Runsheng (nicknamed Short Cai, who also runs a dental inlay shop in the City God Temple) to reason with the Chen family. After mediation, the Chen family agreed to return 50 yuan to Wang as compensation. At the time, 30 yuan was paid, with 20 yuan still owed. It was agreed to meet at the Deyi Teahouse in the City God Temple at 10:00 AM yesterday. Tang Gengquan and Chen Runsheng were called from the Wang family's residence, and Wu Chunzhi, the owner of Huayang Restaurant at 154 Fuyou Road, and an acquaintance of Wu, were invited from the Chen family's residence, along with Chen Xiaomei, to sort out the matter from three sides. Chen Xiaomei handed over 15 yuan to Tang and others, while Tang Gengquan, the representative of Wang, handed over the "eight characters" betrothal card. However, Short Xiao Wang was not present at the time.

Screams for help from the restaurant: After the negotiations were clear, everyone dispersed. Xiaomei went to the Fuxin Tobacco Company on Kangti Road to collect her wages of 1 yuan and 10 cents, and returned to the Huayang Restaurant on Fuyou Road to talk to Wu Chunzhi. Unexpectedly, her former fiancé Short Xiao Wang was already there. Seeing Xiaomei approaching, he also followed her in. He met Wu Chunzhi and spoke a few words to him, then asked Wu to go upstairs for a private talk. Wu did not suspect anything at the time, and the two went upstairs. Xiaomei waited downstairs. Shortly after the two went upstairs, screams of fighting were heard from upstairs, and Wu cried for help.

Blade covered in blood: Before Wu finished calling for help, Xiao Wang had already rushed downstairs in a panic. He was seen holding a six-inch blade in his hand, covered in blood. He ran straight out the door, while Wu also chased after him, trying to confront him. Seeing that the situation was not good, Wang threw the blade aside and fled without a trace. When Wu chased out of the store, he collapsed to the ground from his injuries, covered in blood. Neighbors gathered after hearing the alarm, but only saw that Wu had two knife wounds, one on the left abdomen and one on the right chest. His intestines had spilled out and he died shortly after.

Deceased awaiting autopsy: After the incident, Gao Wanling, a police officer from the 14th post of the 2nd section of the 1st district, arrived after hearing the alarm. However, the murderer had already fled far away. He immediately reported to the police station, and Chief Yi immediately led a team of police officers to the scene for investigation. Chen Xiaomei, the main person involved, and Li Zhenxiang, a friend of the murderer, were arrested and taken to the station for interrogation. The deceased, Wu Chunzhi, was a 31-year-old man from Yangzhou. Huayang Restaurant was opened by him and his friend Chen Lide as a joint venture. The store was opened in January of this year, initially selling wine. Later, due to poor business, it was converted into a noodle restaurant. After the interrogation, Chief Yi immediately ordered the local police chief to report to the court for an autopsy. He also ordered his subordinates to strictly apprehend the murderer and bring him to justice.

Rickshaw Driver Extorts Owner After Being Dismissed

Three letters demanding 30,000 yuan

Meeting arranged on Route Ferguson

Arrested while negotiating

Li Weinong, a native of Changshu, residing at 907 Weihaiwei Road, worked as a clerk at the Anmao Foreign Firm on Jiangxi Road. His monthly income was not substantial, yet he was also targeted by bandits. On April 30th, a letter was sent to Li's residence, stating that the party was experiencing financial difficulties and, upon the order of Commander Ma Yushan, was requesting a loan of 15,000 yuan from him. At the time, Li had already taken leave and returned to his hometown, and his family ignored the matter. On June 12th, the bandits sent another letter to Li, demanding money, but the amount had increased to 30,000 yuan. They also stated that if he was sincere, he should write a blood character on red paper and stick it at the entrance of his residence. Li had already returned to Shanghai from his hometown and sent the two letters to the News Police Station for investigation. The police chief ordered Li to act according to the instructions in the letter to observe the situation. After the red paper was posted, there was no response at first. It was not until the 25th of this month that the bandits replied, saying that the red paper had been seen. They requested that another red paper with the word "True" be written on it and pasted in the original place. They also requested that the money be placed in a straw bag and sent by a person wearing black clothes in a yellow rickshaw to the wilderness at the end of Route Ferguson in the French Concession between 7:00 AM and 9:00 AM on the 27th. Someone would receive it. Li reported the letter to the police again. On the appointed day, the police chief dispatched detectives Deng Jingfan, Yang Xinzheng, Liu Longchao, and others disguised as steelworkers to lie in ambush around the designated location. Li had his servant Zhu Zisheng change into black clothes, carry a straw bag filled with newspapers, and go by rickshaw. Upon arrival, a Chongming man named Huang Huiming came from elsewhere, scrutinized Zhu, looked around, and greeted Zhu. The detectives then arrested Huang and brought him back to the police station. After interrogation, they went to 550 Dalianwan Road and arrested another accomplice named Ji Ziqing. Yesterday morning, both were sent to the Special District Court, where Judge Ge interrogated them. Li Weinong stated the circumstances of receiving the three threatening letters and claimed that Ji Ziqing was originally his rickshaw driver and was dismissed because he had a conflict with the maid on April 13th. Huang Huiming confessed that he had an brother-in-law named Ji Shirong, who was a rickshaw driver for the Xu family at 44 Chongqing Road. On the 26th of this month, he met him on the road and was invited to his home for lunch. Ji Ziqing was also present. After the meal, Shirong asked him to go to his house again the next morning. He went as agreed. Shirong took him to the end of Route Ferguson and stopped, ordering him to go forward to scout for anyone carrying a straw bag. He did not know his intention and went forward alone. He saw a man carrying a straw bag standing on the side of the road. He was about to turn back to report to Shirong, but was arrested. Ji Ziqing denied everything in his confession. Judge Ge stated that the case still needed to be investigated and ordered the two defendants to be detained pending further interrogation on July 7th.

Police Officer Assaults Wife of a Road Worker

Abusing power and committing violence, the road worker is injured

Public outrage leads to dismissal

Yesterday morning, a dispute occurred between a police officer at the Shanghai North Railway Station and a road worker at the station. Fortunately, it was resolved early, and the matter was settled. The day before yesterday (the 28th) was the payday for the station's workers. A road worker named Wu Shengrong had just been transferred from Nanjing Station to work in Shanghai. As he was unfamiliar with everything, he did not know that it was payday that day. When the other road workers informed him, he understood. However, according to the regulations, workers must have their name chop and a salary certificate with a photo to collect their salary. Wu Shengrong had left his at home and asked someone to inform his wife to bring it. He then went outside the station to buy food to satisfy his hunger. When he returned to the train platform, he saw a police officer (No. 33) blocking his wife's path, harassing her. The road worker saw this and immediately questioned the officer, stating that his wife had come to bring the salary certificate and should not be treated lightly. Unexpectedly, the police officer responded with abusive words, falsely accusing them of not being a formal couple and cursing loudly. After a brief argument, the police officer slapped Wu Shengrong several times and then punched and kicked him. As a result, his face and other parts of his body were injured. Everyone present was outraged, believing that police officers and workers both served the railway and should help each other. It was uncalled for to insult the worker for no reason. They sent the injured Wu Shengrong to the railway hospital for examination and treatment and planned to report the matter to the chief of the train station and have the police officer punished. However, the day before yesterday was Sunday, and the railway bureau's offices were closed as usual. Therefore, the workers went on strike at 10:00 AM yesterday and went to see the chief of the train station to report the incident and demand appropriate action. After the two chiefs learned of the incident, they summoned the head of the responsible police division. The head of the division replied to the workers' representatives that the offending police officer would be dismissed immediately. The workers were satisfied and returned to their posts, and the turmoil subsided.

The Shanghai World Buddhist Laymen's Association, considering that the supply of dishes and rice for passengers on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railway dining cars is convenient, but there are also quite a few vegetarians these days. During travel, it's inconvenient because there are no vegetarian options available on the train. Therefore, they suggested to the two railway bureaus the other day that vegetarian meals be provided on each train. The railway bureaus adopted this suggestion and it will be implemented soon.

Anhui Official Allowed to Post Bail

Ordered to return to Anhui to settle accounts

Wang Shaoyi, the magistrate of Lai'an County, Anhui Province, embezzled public funds and fled to Shanghai, staying at the Dadong Hotel on Nanjing Road. The Anhui Provincial Government telegraphed the Shanghai Public Security Bureau to arrest him nearby. He was arrested by Chief Chen of the Public Security Bureau and detectives, along with the officers from the Old Zhabei Police Station. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that Wang's position as magistrate of Lai'an County was relinquished in June of the 18th year of the Republic. The embezzled public funds of 9,727 yuan were also outstanding debts that had not been settled at the time of his departure. Yesterday morning, the police sent Wang to the Special District Court, where Judge Xu held the trial. According to Wang's confession, he left his post first due to other important matters, and all transfer procedures were handled by the accounting director Chen Xianglun on his behalf. He is currently serving as the head of the opium suppression office in Yucheng, Henan. Recently, he received an official letter from the Anhui Provincial Department of Finance, stating that the funds handled during his tenure in Lai'an had not been properly transferred and he was ordered to settle the matter. Therefore, he came to Shanghai from Henan, intending to go to Anhui to clarify that the funds were not embezzled. In fact, he had advanced over 5,000 yuan for the purchase of weapons at the time, and he had also advanced a considerable amount of funds for bandit suppression, which should be used to offset the amount. Judge Xu reviewed the confession and ordered Wang Shaoyi to provide a 10,000 yuan cash bond or a shop bond and return to Anhui to settle the matter himself.

Two Attempt Suicide by Jumping into River Due to Economic Hardship

Both were rescued

Zhu Zhongyi, a 46-year-old local, was alone and worked as a coolie at the Nissin Company wharf in Hongkou to make a living. He was extremely poor and miserable. Recently, due to his age and illness, his work became difficult, leading to a reduction in his income. He often faced the threat of starvation. He felt sorry for himself and became disgusted with life. The day before yesterday afternoon, he boarded sampan No. 1399 at the wharf, claiming to go to Pudong. When they reached the middle of the river, he jumped into the water to commit suicide. Fortunately, the sampan operator rescued him and sent him to the Customs Police Station. After learning of his situation, yesterday they sent him to the Nissin Company coolie foreman, ordering him to find a way to help him.

Bao Heming: Yesterday morning at 12:15, a middle-aged man hired sampan No. 256 at the Guangdong Road wharf, saying he wanted to go to Pudong. The sampan operator sailed towards the other shore as instructed. When they were in the middle of the river, the man suddenly jumped into the water to commit suicide, sinking and then floating again. A British warship was docked nearby, and the sailors on board saw it and immediately launched a motorboat to rescue the man. They notified the Customs Water Police Station by telephone. Detective Wu Rongsheng boarded the ship and took him back to the police station. He confessed that his name was Bao Heming, 22 years old, from Wuxi, and lived at 31 Shunxingfang, Tiantong Temple Road, Zhabei. He committed suicide to end his troubles due to economic hardship. A search of his body revealed only two small yuan and several copper coins. The police officers persuaded him and sent him home, instructing his family to comfort him and ease his mind.

Killed While Jumping Off a Moving Vehicle to Retrieve a Hat

Guo Linfu, a native of Haimen, worked as a coolie at the Songsenji Construction Company on Beijing Road. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, he was transporting wood to Jiangwan in a truck. On the way, Linfu's straw hat was blown away by the wind. Without waiting for the vehicle to stop, Linfu jumped off to retrieve it. Accidentally, he fell and was seriously injured in his lower body. He was sent to the Tongren Hospital for treatment, but died at around 3:00 PM in the afternoon. The hospital reported the death to the Hongkou Police Station, who sent officers to transfer the body to the morgue for an autopsy.

Girl Crushed to Death by Truck

Zhou Guibao, a nine-year-old girl from Funing, residing at 73 Jinling Road, Zhabei, went out for a stroll alone at noon yesterday. While walking in front of Qinyeli, a truck No. 8357 from the Hongji Transportation Company at 279 Yangshupu Road, driven by Zhang Honglin from Yangzhou, was speeding from the west. The driver failed to brake in time and knocked the girl down. The wheels ran over her head and abdomen, causing her flesh to rot and blood to flow all over the ground. She died instantly. Her father, Zhou Risheng, arrived upon hearing the news and mourned greatly over her body. The police officers from the 2nd section of the 4th district arrived at the scene and arrested the driver responsible for the accident and sent him to the police station for investigation.

Young Woman Runs Away, Accuses Husband of Kidnapping

Xu Guoren, police chief of the Jinyi Precinct of the Second Branch of the Sixth District of Xuhui, Shanghai, received a report around 9 PM the night before last from Jiang Wang, a woman from Yancheng. She claimed that in July of the previous autumn, she was threatened with a gun by Zhou Guancheng, a bandit from her hometown, and forcibly brought to Shanghai. She was hidden at No. 7 Yiban Road near Haichao Temple in the Nanshi area. On the 21st of this month, they moved to No. 2614 Heping Li on Xiexu Road, where she was closely guarded day and night and unable to escape. The day before yesterday, taking advantage of a slight lapse in security, she managed to flee. However, she was caught and brought back in the Xiejiao area. Zhou's friend, Qi Yubin, aided and abetted the abuse, locking her up and severely beating her, leaving her covered in bruises. Now, they were planning to sell her off. Therefore, she seized an opportunity to escape last night and sought help. She also stated that Zhou had committed multiple gun-related crimes in their hometown. Police Chief Xu immediately arrested Zhou Guancheng and Qi Yubin, along with Jiang Wang, and sent all three to the station for investigation. After a preliminary hearing conducted by Police Chief Liu, the plaintiff, Jiang Wang, testified that she was 21 years old, from Yancheng, and detailed the events as described above. Zhou Guancheng, 25 years old, also from Yancheng, testified that he made a living as a rickshaw puller. On June 18th of the previous year, through matchmakers Cao Shousheng and Zhou Anbai, he married the daughter of Hu Wenshu in their hometown. They moved to Shanghai in the autumn. However, the plaintiff was extremely promiscuous and did not uphold her wifely duties. On February 26th of this year, at 7 PM, she ran away and eloped. On the 20th of this month, he discovered that the plaintiff had been seduced by Xu Lao San, a worker at the Sanxing Silk Weaving Factory on Meixie Road. He immediately reported this to the factory manager, who suspended Xu. Zhou then took the plaintiff back into his custody, fearing that Xu would entice her again, and moved to Heping Li. He administered a slight beating, hoping she would change her ways. Now, the plaintiff, being reprimanded, was falsely accusing him of being a bandit. Qi Yubin, 27 years old, residing in Qili Lane, west of Haichao Temple, testified that he did not participate in the beating, only slightly admonished her, and knew nothing else about the matter. Based on the testimonies, Police Chief Liu concluded that the accounts of both parties were contradictory, the situation was complex, and the defendants wife had a different surname than the plaintiff. Therefore, he ordered that the plaintiff and defendants be sent to the bureau for further handling.

Zhang Wenrui's Heartbroken Account of Losing Her Virginity

Why is Wang Runlai so heartless?

Zhang Wenrui, a 24-year-old woman from Songjiang, was deeply loved by her parents while they were alive. She was not yet married. Unfortunately, her parents passed away one after another, leaving behind a few acres of thin land. Because she could not cultivate it herself, it gradually became barren, and her livelihood became difficult. Last autumn, the woman came to Shanghai and resided with her relative at No. 42 Deshan Li on Avenue Dubail. She intended to find work as a seamstress. However, she was seduced by Wang Runlai, the son of Wang Jisheng, who owns the Leguzhai Antique Shop in the citys Huayuan Li, and they fell in love. Later, they built a small home in the pavilion of No. 215 Shiyuli on Avenue Eduard VII, living together like husband and wife. Runlai's love for the woman deepened, and they secretly vowed to be together forever. They lived in seclusion for more than half a year, never returning home. All daily expenses were covered by Wenrui, who, believing she was already Runlai's wife, returned to her hometown and sold all her land to support their life together. On May 2nd of the lunar calendar, Runlai was suddenly found by his father

and forced to return home. By the 9th, Runlai had escaped again and was staying with Wenrui in Room 8 of the Huidong Hotel on Avenue Eduard VII. Unexpectedly, the other day, Runlai's legal wife arrived and created a huge scene, violently beating Wenrui. She immediately took Runlai back home. Wenrui, reflecting on her mistake, realized that she had lost her virginity to Runlai, ruining her reputation. The land left by her parents had been sold off. She was also four months pregnant. Now, she had suffered this humiliation. Looking ahead, her future seemed bleak and uncertain. She conceived the idea of suicide, weeping all night. Yesterday morning, she went out and bought a large amount of opium, secretly swallowed it, and lay crying on the bed, tears streaming down her face. A waiter named A Si noticed through a crack in the window and immediately reported it to the front desk, who managed to open the room. They found Wenrui covered in vomit and immediately rushed her to Renji Hospital. After receiving injections and treatment from the doctor, she remained in critical condition. The hospital reported the incident to the police, who dispatched a detective to the hospital to investigate. Later, in Room 8 of the Huidong Hotel, they found a suicide note written by Wenrui, addressed to Wang Runlai, in which her words were extremely sad. It is unknown whether she will survive.

Tang Wanzhen Injured by Nitric Acid

Tang Wanzhen, a woman from Haimen residing at No. 52 Tongxing Road in Wusong, was in her early twenties and quite beautiful. Last year, she married a man named Yuan from the same village. However, due to differences of opinion, they separated this spring. Unexpectedly, around 9:20 the night before last, as Wanzhen was walking past the Tianlun Silk and Satin Bureau on Songxing Road, a person suddenly jumped out from the shadows, holding a bottle of nitric acid, and poured it on Wanzhen's head. The person, seeing that their goal was achieved, fled. Wanzhen collapsed from the pain and was taken to the Haibin Hospital on Wusong Wai Ma Road for treatment. Her face was severely injured and completely swollen, with signs of ulceration. It is feared that it will take a long time to heal. The reason for the incident is believed to be jealousy, leading someone to resort to such a cruel act.

Anhui Su County Reports Disaster, Appeals for Relief

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee received an official letter from the Su County Hail Disaster Relief Committee in Anhui Province. It stated: "We weep with sorrow, for misfortune has befallen the people of Su County, with repeated major disasters. Last year, when the wheat was about to ripen, it was damaged by wind. In the autumn, there was a major flood, which inundated much of the farmland. This spring, before the harvest, 90% of the population lacked food. Sources were scarce, and there was no way to buy it. In the cities, relief in the form of rice and flour was available, but it could not alleviate the high price of flour. In the countryside, people subsisted on weeds, which barely provided enough to eat. They could only barely survive, waiting for the season to change. As summer approached, we rejoiced at the prospect of harvesting the wheat, which was about to ripen, and thought that we would soon have enough to eat. Unexpectedly, the heavens unleashed another disaster, a catastrophic event. Suddenly, on the afternoon of May 31st, hail fell, lasting for about an hour. Some hailstones were as small as goose eggs, others as large as rice bowls, and some were even the size of soccer balls. The ground was covered to a depth of several inches. From the northwest to the southeast, the area affected was about twenty li wide and one hundred li long. In all districts of the county, the wheat crop was completely destroyed. All the wheat stalks were scattered by the wind and carried away by the flood, benefiting only the birds. Only the roots, barely an inch above the ground, remained. Not only was the food that was about to be harvested snatched away, but firewood and cattle feed were also gone. The newly planted autumn seedlings were also destroyed. Furthermore, the wind added to the devastation, blowing off roofs and sending tiles flying. People and animals died in the fields, piled on top of each other. People were struck dead by the hail, blown into ditches, and their bodies were revealed as the ice melted. There were such scenes everywhere. With no hope of a wheat harvest and no ability to plant autumn crops, small landowners were instantly reduced to poverty, and poor families considered suicide. As a result, people were displaced and wandered along the roads, with children wailing and women crying, a constant sound in the air. The tragic situation is all true, without any exaggeration. It is an unprecedented disaster. Therefore, we have publicly appointed representatives Ma Xiaotang and Chen Haishan to visit and personally present our case, imploring you to provide relief to save these disaster-stricken people."

Invention of the "Standard Exposure Meter"

The greatest challenge in photography lies in accurate exposure. Gao Weixiang and Lin Zewei, recognizing this, have conducted extensive experiments both domestically and internationally over the past five to six years. Through careful research, they have invented the "Standard Exposure Meter." The meter is extremely easy to use; even children can operate it. With a single movement, it provides the correct exposure time (totaling 132 variations) and aperture for various scenes and lighting conditions. It can also be used to determine the exposure time and aperture for moving picture cameras. Compared to all other exposure meters in the world, it is far superior in terms of quality and convenience, making it a significant contribution to the field of photography. It is reported that the meter has been translated into English and patent applications have been filed abroad. It is currently exclusively manufactured and sold by the China Photography Supply Company at No. 56 Nanjing Road. Made of transparent faux ivory, it is priced at only 80 cents per meter.

Jin Jiulin, a detective inspector from the French Concession Special Agency, along with detectives Li Yaolong and Tang Yunqing, deputy detectives Qian Yumin, Mao Jingen, Lu Zhulin, and Zhang Ziji, and patrolman Zhou Buguang, discovered that thieves were hiding in Room 26 of the Xin Zhonghua Inn in Hongyunfang, Rue Wagner. Chaussée, Qiu Kunmao at No. 6 Ping'anfang, Rue Massenet, and Shen Huating at No. 73 Ande Li, Rue Lan Wei Li, admitting to three robberies. They were ordered to be detained. Shen Yufu said that although he did discuss with Shi Chengwen, he did not know they were thieves and asked for a fair trial. News from Various Labor Unions

Various Labor Unions: The Fifth District Cigarette Industry Union, Municipal Postal Workers Union, Fifth District Shipbuilding Industry Union, Fifth District Cotton Weaving Industry Union, Preparatory Committee of the Municipal Wooden Boat Industry Union, Preparatory Committee of the Municipal Local Yellow Wine Industry Union, Preparatory Committee of the Fifth District Match Industry Union, Preparatory Committee of the Fifth District Carpentry Industry Union, and more than 40 other labor unions issued a declaration against the Jinxin Factory's oppression of workers. It stated that the Jinxin Cloth Factory in Nanshi has dismissed workers without cause. Although the Social Affairs Bureau has mediated several times, the factory has refused to accept the mediation and has not indicated any intention to submit to arbitration. The government's order to reinstate the workers should have been strictly implemented, but for two months, the factory has defied the order. Recently, it has even used force to prevent workers from entering the factory for food and lodging. These unions believe that the employer's actions are extremely illegal. In addition to expressing unlimited sympathy for the workers of the factory, they hope that the authorities will quickly mediate impartially to avoid causing unemployment and will impose severe sanctions on employers who violate government orders, in order to maintain labor rights and serve as a warning to those who disregard laws. This declaration is hereby issued.

The First District Cotton Weaving Industry Labor Union issued a declaration yesterday, stating that the Jinxin Cloth Factory, out of resentment for workers joining the labor union, dismissed worker representatives Yao Zushun and six others without cause on May 4th, cutting off their food and lodging and expelling them from the factory. During the several mediations by the Social Affairs Bureau, the employer showed no sincerity and offered no reasonable explanation. After the order to reinstate the workers, they did not comply and did not raise any objections. When the Social Affairs Bureau forwarded a letter to the Public Security Bureau for enforcement, the employer, in conjunction with the industry association, filed a complaint against Wang Shui of the Social Affairs Bureau by express mail and telegram. At that time, in order to avoid escalating the labor unrest, the union, together with the industry association, reached a settlement. However, the union made concessions while the other party raised their demands. As a result, the settlement fell apart. Later, the municipal government approved the Public Security Bureau to enforce the order again. After several attempts to send police escorts to reinstate the workers, they were forcibly expelled. Since then, two months have passed. During these two months, innocent workers have suffered from unemployment, hunger, and cold. They have pawned everything and have no way to borrow money. Their appearance is emaciated and miserable. However, the union and the workers have endured until now, waiting for the government to investigate and deal with the matter according to law. Now, the employer treats government laws as child's play, disregarding the workers' lives. This is not only unreasonable, but also inhumane. In order to protect the interests of the workers and implement government laws, the union is determined to sacrifice and fight to the death. Because its power is limited, it hopes that all sectors of society will provide assistance to maintain the credibility of the government and relieve the workers' suffering. This declaration is hereby issued.

The Laundry Industry Labor Union held a reorganization meeting yesterday, attended by more than 400 members. Chen Shouqing presided over the meeting. The following items were discussed: (1) Adoption of the labor union constitution. Resolution: Amended and adopted. (2) Amendment of the labor-management conditions and working hours. Resolution: Adopted and handed over to the council for handling. (3) Restriction on excessive apprenticeship fees. Resolution: Merged into the previous case. (4) Omitted. Then, the election began. As a result, Chen Shouqing, Zhou Linfu, Ni Shanqing, Jiang Fusheng, Zhang Dingxing, Yuan Mingshui, and He Xuehong were elected as directors, and Chen Yuxiang, Yu Cheng, and Gu Lianfa were elected as supervisors.

The Letterpress Printing Industry Labor Union held its first supervisory committee meeting the other evening. Qian Shuntao, the chairman, reported the purpose of the meeting: (1) Shen Xueru proposed the following regarding accounting matters: 1. All accounts from the preparatory period to the end of June should be transferred to the supervisory committee for review. 2. Starting from July 1st, all income, except for the accounting department of the union, must be submitted to the accounting department for registration within 24 hours to ensure prudence. All payments must go through the accounting department. (2) Qian Shuntao proposed that all personnel responsible for the union's work must report each item for verification. The Nanshi Transportation Branch requested to join the union. After review, it was resolved to approve it and the secretariat would send a letter to the branch. (3) Qian Shuntao proposed that the union's registration procedures had been completed long ago, but the seal had not yet been received, so a representative should be sent to collect it as soon as possible. (4) Shen Xueru proposed that personnel attending external events on behalf of the union must be designated by the board of directors and supervisors. Resolution: Passed. (5) Qian Shuntao proposed that the issue of revising the labor-management contract had been shelved for too long and should be resolved within a short period of time. The meeting adjourned at 9:00 PM.
