Free Talk

Gleanings from the Country

— Shi Nong

The Qiantang River cannot be crossed at night. If crossed at night, winds and waves will surely arise, leading to the danger of capsizing. Even tugboats cannot avoid this. To this day, no one dares to cross it at night.

The Qiantang tidal bore is highest in mid-July, doubling the height of the full moon tide in August. However, it is a chaotic tide. The reliable tide in August features thousands of bright lights floating on the water surface at night (mostly placed by people near the opposite bank), moving back and forth with the tide. During the day, hundreds and thousands of seabirds can be seen flying in flocks a hundred zhang ahead of the tidal bore.

There are no mosquitoes in Fengyang. Legend has it that mosquitoes avoid the imperial edict of Zhu Yuanzhang.

The frogs within the city of Jinan do not croak. If frogs from within the city are taken outside the city, their croaking is deafening. If frogs from outside the city are brought inside, they fall silent again.

In the Three Gorges of the Yangtze River, within the Military Books and Precious Swords Gorge, one can see a red box within the thousand-foot cliffs. It is said to have been placed by Zhuge Liang, containing military books and precious swords. To this day, many have tried to retrieve it but have failed.

In the Zhang Fei Temple within the city of Yunyang, Sichuan, Zhang Fei's head is stored in an oil well behind the altar. If dozens of catties of vegetable oil are added, it will rise above the well opening and become visible.

Wu Peifu's Journey Out of Sichuan

— Cheng Junsong

News of Wu Peifu's departure from Sichuan has been circulating for a long time, but it has recently faded into silence. Perhaps news from Sichuan is slow to arrive? Recently, a friend came from Chengdu and provided a detailed account of Wu's movements. I will quickly record it below.

After his military defeat, Wu Peifu retreated to eastern Sichuan. The years passed by, and two years have already passed. His former ambitions have been worn away, and he now only cultivates flowers and reads paintings. His desolate situation is almost like that of Du Shaoling (Du Fu) when he depended on Yan Wu. Recently, he felt a lack of interest in living under someone else's roof and longed to return to his native Penglai to rest and recuperate. Moreover, he has become a figure of the past in politics, and no faction harbors any suspicion towards him. Therefore, with the consent of the central government, he was allowed to leave Sichuan. Wu packed his belongings and, with his wife and over 400 staff members, set off from Xiaba Temple Town in Xuanhan County on May 13th. The next day, he arrived in Suiding. A certain gentleman paid a visit and, after a pleasant conversation, presented him with a single piece of calligraphy in cursive script, which read, "One year to plant grain, ten years to plant trees, a hundred years to cultivate people, a thousand years to cultivate virtue." Below, it was inscribed, "Aiming for the top, you only get the middle; aiming for the middle, you only get the bottom; aiming for the bottom, you get nothing at all." From this, Wu's breadth of mind can be seen. He stayed in Suiding for several days and then, on the 24th, went to Guang'an. He arrived on the 26th. The area is under the control of Yang Sen, and Yang sent personnel to take care of and protect him along the way. When I (the friend speaking) left Sichuan, Wu was still there and seemed to not have departed yet. As for Wu's subsequent journey, it is said that he will take the route through Shunqing and Tongchuan to Chengdu, then from Chengdu to Qingcheng Mountain and Emei Mountain. He plans to visit Emei Mountain for ten days, to explore the beauty of the mountains and rivers, and then take the route through Jiading, Xufu, Luzhou, Chongqing, and Wanxian, traveling by boat to Yichang. From there, he will pass through Wuhan and the capital, arriving in Shanghai, visiting West Lake in Hangzhou, and then returning to Penglai. Based on the time, if there are no unexpected obstacles, he should be able to shake hands with people in Shanghai in July.

Also, during the Lantern Festival in my hometown, there is often a practice of hanging tiger lanterns and guessing riddles. There are two telegrams about Wu that are relevant to this article. One is "Wu Peifu's Recent Situation," with the riddle being a Tang poem: "Now it is not like the time in Luoyang." The other is "Wu Peifu Regains Momentum," with the riddle being a passage from Zuo Zhuan: "The son arrived to restore the army." The former expresses regret for Wu's desolate situation, while the latter predicts Wu's comeback. However, from the perspective of Wu, who has experienced so much hardship, he probably no longer has such thoughts.

Record of the American Newspaper Industry Film Screening

— Huang Jiping

In recent years, publications in our country have gradually flourished. The creation of newspapers has spread from urban areas to the interior. News education has also gradually gained attention. For example, universities have established journalism departments and formed journalism associations, and have sent personnel abroad to specialize in journalism or to investigate the newspaper industry. This is truly a dawn for the newspaper industry's future. We can generally talk about the development of the newspaper industry in various countries. However, what we know is based on hearsay rather than personal observation. The actual situation is not something that those who have not experienced it firsthand can fully understand. This time, Mr. Powell, the Shanghai-based reporter for the Chicago Tribune (and also the chief writer for the Miller's Review of the Far East), specially introduced a photographic film of the newspaper, "From Trees to Tribunes," which was screened in Shanghai to meet with our press. This allows us to know a glimpse of the American newspaper industry. His kindness is truly commendable.

After the film was transported to Shanghai, Mr. Powell wrote to the Shanghai Newspaper Association to preside over the event. This association is the central hub of various newspapers, aiming to increase the benefits of those in the press. They selected the Nanjing Grand Theater to hold the screening at 11:30 a.m. on the 28th, and gave tickets to employees of Chinese and foreign newspapers, news agencies, advertising companies, and those not in the press. At that time, attendance was extremely enthusiastic, with about 1,500 Chinese and foreign dignitaries. Mr. Kong Xiangxi also attended. It is said that there were two sections in the film about afforestation and papermaking, which are closely related to the Ministry of Industry. Mr. Kong's arrival may have been for this reason. At the time of the screening, Mr. Wang Yingbin of Shen Bao broadcasted via radio, first thanking Mr. Powell and the theater owner for their kind intentions, and then translating the main ideas of the film.

The film is divided into three reels. The first reel shows mountains and forests, with dense shade covering the sky. Workers with axes or saws enter the forest to cut down trees, which are cut into segments and thrown into streams. They flow down with the rapids, reaching the harbor and then being transported to the newspaper's own paper mill. The second reel shows the papermaking process. First, the wood is ground into sawdust by machine, mixed with chemical agents, and turned into wood pulp. After several refining and remanufacturing processes, it becomes fine, clean newsprint, which is transported to the newspaper office, all the way until it is put into the printing press. The third reel shows the work inside the newspaper office. There are many people in the editorial department, and the work is intense. The completed drafts are sent to the typesetting room. Typesetting is also done mechanically, like typing. Other departments, such as composing, paper cutting, copper plate casting, lead plate casting, and printing, work incredibly fast. After the newspapers are printed, they are automatically transported to the distribution department. Newspaper vendors, at the break of dawn, brave the stars and the moon, rushing to the market to sell newspapers. Another part goes directly from the printing press to the packaging room, also using machines for packaging, in preparation for sending to the post office for mailing. Those transported by boat or vehicle are all packed and sent to the station, port, or airport. Seeing the convenience of transportation, one realizes the close relationship between transportation and life. This newspaper sells over one million copies daily, and doubles that on Sundays. Its grand scale and perfect organization go without saying. Even considering the newspaper office building, the forty-plus-story building soars into the clouds, magnificent and majestic, making people feel a sense of awe.

Interesting Anecdotes About Matches

— Lü Bing

The matches we use daily are commonly called "foreign fire" or "self-igniting fire," probably because this item originally came from overseas, hence the addition of the word "foreign." Matches have traditionally been divided into red-tipped and black-tipped. Black-tipped matches are safer, and it is not easy to ignite them without rubbing them hard. However, when the box is full of matches, if the lid is not tightly closed, and one takes out a match and rubs it against the exposed head on the side of the box, in dry weather, a little carelessness can easily cause the entire box to catch fire, burning one's fingers. Even if one waves one's hand quickly, it is not easy to get rid of it. Many of my friends have suffered skin burns due to slight carelessness. This is also something that match users should pay attention to. Red-tipped matches contain the most phosphorus and are even more dangerous. In recent years, they have gradually become less common in the market. According to a British magazine, there is an interesting anecdote about the cessation of red-tipped match production in that country.

This matter was mentioned by Mr. Riddell, a member of the British Parliament, in a recent speech to the Public Health Committee. He said that the earliest matches contained a high amount of phosphorus. Phosphorus is not only highly explosive, but also easily enters the human body during its preparation, causing phosphorus necrosis and severely eroding the bones. One of Mr. Riddell's friends was an expert in match manufacturing. When he was young, he occasionally followed his father to visit the match factory. He was greatly shocked by a dark room. In a corner of the room sat a worker, his face glowing brightly in the darkness, a terrifying sight. Upon inquiry, he learned that the worker had been working for many years and was deeply poisoned by phosphorus. All the bones of his face had absorbed phosphorus, resulting in this phenomenon. Feeling sympathy, the friend later inherited his father's business and immediately decided to stop the production of red-tipped matches, repeatedly stating their harms in order to obtain the consent of other companies in the industry. The public, after being promoted by him, also refrained from using them. For a time, red-tipped matches disappeared from the British market.

Groundbreaking Ceremony for Martyr Xiong Chengji's Memorial Park

— Ming

Martyr Xiong Chengji of Jiangdu raised an army in Anqing and died for his cause in Dong Province. More than twenty years have passed. Now, under the request of Central Committee member Wang Boling and others, the Central Government and the Provincial Government have suggested building a shrine at the Guanyuan Garden on the shore of Slender West Lake in Yangzhou. The groundbreaking ceremony was held on June 28th. A posthumous portrait of the martyr when he was captured in Harbin has been found, along with a short biography to introduce him to the people of the country.

The martyr's given name was Chengji, courtesy name Weigen, from Jiangdu. He graduated from the Naval Artillery Academy's officer training program. In the thirty-fourth year of the Guangxu reign of the fallen Qing Dynasty, the martyr was a team officer in the 9th Artillery Battalion. He raised an army in Anqing during the autumn maneuvers, fled to Tongcheng, went to Qingdao, and crossed over to Japan. In the first year of the Xuantong reign, he arrived in Changchun, changing his name to Yi Longqian, courtesy name Wangyun, planning a major uprising. He resided with the Zang Guan San families. Zang came from banditry, and his son, Keming, conspired with him in Japan. Guan San repeatedly extorted money from him. He then went to Harbin. Just as Prince Qing Xun returned from Europe, the martyr planned to assassinate him on the way. Guan San informed the authorities, and he was arrested. This was on the twenty-fourth day of the twelfth month of the lunar calendar before the founding of the Republic of China. He died for his cause in Jilin Province the following year. He was only twenty-four years old. His coffin was placed in the Sanjiang Guild Hall. In the second year of the Republic of China, he was finally buried at the foot of Pingshan Hall in Jiangdu. Now that the Party-State has been established, more than twenty years have passed, and those who visit the martyr's tomb only feel a sense of fragrant grass in the evening sun, almost forgetting the martyr Xiong, who had the indomitable spirit of the first uprising. Therefore, there is something to be admired.

Travelogue to India (57)

— Ling Hua

Speaking of Gandhi's movement, the Muslims also very much approve of it, saying that it has been quite successful. The villagers can also resist taxes. For example, the salt tax originally did not allow the poor to sell salt. Now this system has been broken, and the British government can do nothing. People can freely sell salt, and the government has difficulty managing it one by one. Tax resistance also exists in various places. As far as I know, people are very free in various parts of Myanmar. The same is true in India, because indirect management is quite difficult to be thorough. I heard that the Siamese government's management is quite strict because it is direct management. I see the matter of the Muslims fasting. Some people are very serious about it depending on their personalities, while others are not. I met a student who bought fruit in the garden and gave me two pieces, keeping two for himself. I asked why he wasn't eating now. He replied that he had to wait until evening to eat because he was fasting during the day. He seemed very serious. But others ate breakfast, eating with me, showing that it is not easy to be uniform. Speaking of the conflicts between Indians and Muslims, the Indian laws are very high and pure, maintaining themselves and not interacting with others. In contrast, I have never heard of conflicts in Chinese Islam, because they have assimilated. Indian religions are noble and strict. Not only do they not intermarry with others, but they also do not socialize with others. It is very difficult to practice their custom of worshiping cows. No matter how noble, it is difficult to promote it everywhere. I respect and pity them, but it is difficult to learn from them.

India is peaceful, and the people are content and obedient. The shops do not have outer walls, and they are scattered. At night, there is no door to close. Everything is free. If you were in China, you couldn't take a step. Those who live in India for a long time become peaceful. The city is clean, and the roads are wide and new, like Lahore. The Westerners are good at governing the city government but not good at governing the countryside. This is why the farmers and workers are poor and start revolutions.

On the 21st, several professors from the Mathematics Society, including Benay Char, invited me to dinner. There was also a Frenchman. The Frenchman was very weak, not at all like the French people in our ideals, who should all be like Napoleon. Benay Char is a talented woman. She showed me that she belongs to the new Protestant sect in India, which does not adhere to the old sect. They have created a copper badge with a lotus flower, a swastika, the letter "A," and a crescent moon, indicating that it is a religion of universal harmony. This sect is quite popular in India today. I told the members that I like mathematics, physics, and philosophy, but I cannot be a true student of mathematics because I am very afraid of it. I heard that there was a flower exhibition, but I couldn't go.

One thing worth noting in this city is that the street names on each street are made in very large characters and engraved on the roadside. The street signs in the streets I have passed in various countries are not clear, not even as good as Shanghai and Nanjing, but this city is special, making it very convenient for pedestrians to recognize. However, there are only numbers on the doorplates and no street names, which is still inconvenient. That day, a businessman, Mr. Liu Songchu, came to invite me again. I see that the young people love to read and have ideas.

Rotary Club Story

??? (7)

— Xu Zhuodai

Zi Liang saw that she was going to pester him again and wouldn't leave, and became anxious: "Hurry up and go downstairs! I'm hungry, I haven't eaten anything since I got up early in the morning. Have you prepared the porridge?"

Upon hearing this, the wife showed a surprised expression and looked at her husband:

"You want to eat porridge?"

"Why wouldn't I want to eat?"

"That's strange! I just ladled the porridge downstairs, and kept calling you down to eat, but you ignored me. I finished the porridge all by myself, and now you suddenly want to eat it."

"Then, what do I eat? Starve?"

Zi Liang got angry, his face flushed red, his stomach rumbling. At this moment, the wife suddenly laughed: "Haha! Are you not a child? You get angry when you hear there's nothing to eat? Don't worry! Your beloved wife, Ms. Yueru, definitely can't bear to let you go hungry. When the nanny comes back, I'll have her buy you some snacks to eat!"

"Are there any crackers left?"

Zi Liang's anger subsided a little, and the wife smiled sweetly again:

"Crackers? There are only meat ones, do you want them or not?"

"Meat ones?"

"The crackers have weevils in them, haven't they become meat crackers?"

"That's outrageous!"

"They're very delicious!"

The wife giggled, and Zi Liang turned his head away, ignoring her. The wife then took a step forward:

"Old Man Wang's obituary says the wake is the day after tomorrow. What kind of gift should we send?"

"A funeral couplet!"

"You always send funeral couplets. A funeral couplet is only worth forty cents. How can you give it away? When my father died, you, the son-in-law in mourning, also sent a funeral couplet."

Zi Liang became impatient and stood up, waving his hand:

"Downstairs..."

Diverging Trends in the Flour Market

Yesterday, after the flour market opened in the morning, it initially showed a flat trend, followed by signs of firmness. Foreign wheat quotations fluctuated by one or two jiao. Although gold prices initially fell, they subsequently rebounded, thus stabilizing public sentiment. Futures for all months, particularly from August onward, rose steadily due to frequent absorption by Tianjin-Yingkou groups. July was particularly favorable due to the halt in selling by factories, naturally boosting outside interest. However, by the afternoon opening, the trends between near and distant months underwent a major shift. As this month was the last day, "浮多" (speculators) were eager to settle their positions, causing the price to gradually decline from 2.025 taels, reaching a low of 2 taels. After the fifth board, prices rebounded slightly. Due to the nature of this month, July futures also softened. However, it was reported that a certain factory had made purchases, resulting in a stagnant situation. Perhaps this kind of action will lead to a bullish trend and further selling plans, which remains to be seen. As for the "兵船现粉" (powdered flour on a military ship), it was said that real buyers were purchasing according to standards, with ordinary flour being priced one fen higher. As a result, this month's prices fell by 1.5 fen compared to the previous day, July remained unchanged, September was up by 7.5 li, October was up by 1 fen, and November was up by 1.25 li.

Not Optimistic About the Wheat Market

Yesterday, wheat futures continued to decline gradually. Since the sharp fall in gold prices, foreign wheat prices have shown little sign of rising. It seems that overseas wheat markets have not yet escaped the period of oversupply. Moreover, after the arrival of new wheat, factory demand has been sluggish, and current wheat inventories in Shanghai have reached 30,000 to 40,000 bags. Given all these factors, bullish investors are naturally nervous. Furthermore, in the past few days of the previous week, approximately 100,000 tons of foreign wheat were transacted. Therefore, the unfavorable prospects for the wheat market are unavoidable due to the prevailing conditions. During both the morning and afternoon sessions, prices gradually fell as bullish investors engaged in reverse selling. Fortunately, the Shaoxing group provided support in the afternoon, slightly stabilizing the market. As a result, July and August futures fell by six fen compared to the previous week, September fell by four fen, October fell by three fen, and November fell by four fen. In the spot wheat market, Shanghai factories have not yet shown demand and are taking a wait-and-see approach. It is rare to see such a scenario during the peak season for new wheat. Throughout the city, only the Ningbo group purchased 400 bags of Nanjing wheat at 3.36 taels.

Decreasing Prices in Wuyuan Young Tea Market

After the new Wuyuan young tea came out, the brokers eagerly purchased it, raising the market price to 7 jiao per jin. Some tea firms even offered 80 yuan for the purchase. This was because the quality of this year's young tea was very good, with tender and fragrant characteristics, and there were many fine goods available. Therefore, the firms were happy to purchase it despite the high price. However, yesterday, a telegram from Shanghai reported that the price of Tunxi Zhenmei tea had fallen by 50 to 60 taels, causing a decrease in the interest of tea firms. The purchase price of young tea today has fallen by 50 yuan per dan, down 20 yuan from the previous two days, and there is still a downward trend.

New Information on Tunxi Tea Market

Since Tunxi tea firms shipped the new "头字" Zhenmei tea to Shanghai and earned over 300 taels, general tea brokers have greatly increased their purchases, raising the market price by over 80 yuan. Brokers from Wudong and Xiuzhuan "四响" (well-known tea producing area) transported their inventories to Tunxi for sale, taking advantage of the high prices in Tunxi. Recently, the market prices announced by various tea firms still range from 70 to 84 or 85 yuan. The original new and old tea firms have all opened their operations as usual, with no increase or decrease compared to last year. The selling price of banknotes has shown a decline, as there is less demand for silver dollars in the tea market. The cost of transporting silver has surged, with the price of 1,000 taels rising from 1,340 yuan to over 1,370 yuan. Sales of tea dust in shops and tea estates have recently been very brisk, with the price per dan rising from 12 yuan to 28 yuan or 30 yuan, the highest record ever. General tea brokers have all switched to purchasing tea dust, and the briskness of sales is rare.

Pitou Yuanzhi Tribute Cloth Prices Increasingly Expensive

The market price of Yuan Qing Tribute Cloth has increased significantly in recent days, as the price of wool overseas has soared, making the fixed price very expensive. Compared to the current spot price, it is a reverse situation. Those holding goods are raising prices, disregarding the insufficient cost. According to the investigation, the inventory of Yuan Qing Tribute Cloth in local and foreign warehouses in Shanghai is very small, especially the five- or six-tael cloths, which are particularly scarce. Yesterday, Rongtai's 15330 Lide Picture was sold for 7.55 taels per yard, Ningfeng's 288 Diamond was 7 taels, Anlijv's Bon was 7 taels net, Tianxiang's 888 was 6.75 taels, De's 2488 Four Virtues was 5 taels, and 1440 Huang Tianba was 5.75 taels.

Sugar Market Reopens Vigorously

Taigu Sugar Also Opens Over 10,000 Bags

Yesterday, there was still a lack of news from the sugar production areas. The association's market price for the 24th grade of coarse white sugar in the Dutch market remained low, and the price remained at 11.2 taels. The 20th grade of medium white sugar was 10.065 taels, and the 8th grade was also 9.25 taels. The market situation was stable, and there was a considerable amount of Japanese sugar trading, and the market also rose slightly. "N" mark was 10.0825 to 85 taels, "SH" mark was 10.06 to 25 taels, "T" mark was 11.2 taels, TM mark was 10.07 taels, TK mark was 10.085 taels, YR mark was 10.05 June 25 to 75, and the trend was quite good. Taigu Sugar sold more than 10,000 bags for delivery in July. The price of DY mark was 4.5 Japanese yen, CW mark was 4.6 yen, B mark was 4.7 yen, HX mark was 4.4 yen, HM mark was 4.2 yen. Meiji Sugar continued to open 10,000 bags in September, and the price of YT mark was 4.5 yuan. The Central Factory opened ARAE at 4.6 yuan for delivery in August and September, and then continued to open 3,000 bags in September at the original price. Dali Sugar also opened 15,000 bags, with the "N" mark price at 4.6 yuan and the "T" mark price at 4.8 yuan. The market was relatively flat. Dutch sugar was sold by the new factory for shipment in August, with the 8th grade of Dutch red sugar at 5.1 Dutch guilders per 100 tons and the 10th grade at 5.27 Dutch guilders. Demand was very quiet. Nanshenglong sold dozens of tons of 8th grade Dutch sugar for delivery in July, priced at 5.075 Dutch guilders, all new regulations plus tax, and the market situation was relatively good.

Scarce Arrival of Longkou Vermicelli in North-South Goods Market Leads to Price Increase

Although over a thousand pieces of Longkou vermicelli arrived a few days ago, most of them were transferred to other places. The number of goods self-managed by local businesses and the number of customer goods was only about 500 pieces. The customer market was very tight, and it was heard that the price was 23 taels, about two taels higher than before, so the market price also followed closely.

New Shipment of French West Nails Arrives in Hardware Market

As reported earlier in this newspaper, the local inventory of French West nails is very low, but there are many buyers, resulting in most of those seeking delivery being unable to purchase. A significant amount of new goods arrived in the past two days, with Gonghexing, Mitsubishi, and other warehouses each receiving two to three thousand barrels. Therefore, buyers, hearing this news, are all making purchases separately. It is heard that over 1,300 barrels have already been sold. The market price is 9.5 taels per barrel. It has been found that most of the buyers are from the Yangtze River region.

Sales of British Steel Plate Driven by Qingyan Region in Hardware Market

Due to the sluggish spot sales in the hardware trade, the market remains lackluster. However, the trend of British steel plates, which have been in the doldrums for a long time, was driven yesterday by the purchase of Qingyan groups, causing the market to be very lively. Prices were rising successively, with increases of two to three qian. For example, 2.5 li is estimated at 8.75 taels per dan, 0.5 fen is 7 taels, 7.5 li is 6.75 taels, 1 fen is 6.25 taels, and prices above 1.5 fen are uniformly sold at 6 taels. According to the investigation, the groups from Qingdao and Yantai purchased a total of 800 to 900 dan yesterday. In addition, groups from the Yangtze River and Tianjin also made some purchases, so the future trend is very promising.

Miscellaneous News: 3,800 Pieces of Tobacco Leaves Shipped from the United States

1,100 pieces of bank note paper shipped from New York, 2,600 barrels of machine oil shipped from North America, 450 tons of tea shipped to North America and Europe, 300 bags of seeds, 40 pieces of yellow silk shipped from southern Anhui, 8,400 bags of cane sugar shipped to the Yangtze River, 200,000 silver dollars shipped to Hankou, 1,300 pieces of Pitu foreign cloth shipped from Japan, 110 pieces of Jinshan squid arrived yesterday, with the price on the market opening at 3.5 taels. According to Ningbo news, the market price of yellow croaker glue has risen to over 200 yuan.

Shanghai Market

Market News

Yianju at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Shimen Road declares: Our ice cream products have won the first prize from the Public Works Department's Health Bureau for many years. Eating it is beneficial to health, and every day we use specially selected fresh fruits, supervised by the owner, meticulous, clean, fresh and beautiful, unmatched. This is recognized by Shanghai people. Now the ice cream is on the market again, with more than ten varieties such as cream, grape, jackfruit, cocoa, and lemon every day, and also selling other frozen drinks and soda items. Also, a large batch of fragrant cloud gauze specially made in Guangdong has arrived. Unwilling to use advertising to promote, so we are particularly self-restrained and selling at low prices. Recently, there has been a large crowd of people buying and drinking iced drinks.

Haining Foreign Firm on Zhaofeng Road declares: Our firm has been engaged in import and export for a long time, and recently also operates confectionery. Last year, we held a "Sweetheart Candy Prize Ticket Competition," and for a time, no less than ten million people heard the news and sent in their entries. Now the prize tickets were drawn in public at the Beijing Grand Theater in this city on the 8th of this month. The first prize was won by Mr. Li Zeshen, worth 1,000 foreign dollars; the second prize was won by Mr. Liu Wenbin, worth 300 foreign dollars; and the third prize was won by Mr. Shen Fugang, worth 100 foreign dollars. Since the prize ticket event was held, the purchase of the candy has been exceptionally crowded.

The Mei Yi Appreciation Society states: Our society recently released new products, including Santa Claus, Cupid, Little Laborer, Seashore Poem, Newly Bathed Large Nude, and new reclining, standing, and sitting styles, as well as the original ones, totaling more than 200 styles. They are all works by famous artists, displayed and sold at the New World National Goods Bazaar, and distributed at Sincere, Wing On, and Xihu Silk Weaving Landscape Factory on North Sichuan Road and other large department stores. Beautifully decorated, they can be called new and unique gifts.

Qingyun Pavilion Commercial Hall on 4th Ma Road declares: In order to increase entertainment for guests, our commercial hall has opened a "Little Guanghan Palace" on the third floor starting from July 1st, gathering famous Shanghai courtesans to sing Beijing-style tunes and popular songs. The time is from 3:00 PM to 7:00 PM and from 8:00 PM to 12:00 AM every day. The tea fee will not be increased.

Kefa Pharmacy on Nanjing Road declares: Our pharmacy has been open for a long time and is very large in scale. The medicines produced are particularly effective. Among them is a kind of "asthma cigarette," which is shaped like an ordinary paper cigarette. It can relieve asthma, reduce phlegm, and regulate qi. The effect is very fast. If elderly people are overworked and experience asthma, they can put one in their mouth and immediately feel comfortable. It is indeed worthy of being an "asthma savior."

Daxin Silk and Satin Shop at the corner of 3rd Ma Road and Shimen Road declares: Our shop previously imported a large batch of modern clothing materials. Later, people from all walks of life, socialites, daughters of noble families, and young students went to purchase them one after another. All the goods with novel patterns and low prices, such as woven flower georgette, woven flower voile, woven flower silk, poplin, and Indian silk, were quickly sold out and became popular in the market. There was a risk of some goods running out. Fortunately, the staff of the shop were quick and thorough in their work, and they telegraphed famous domestic factories in advance to expedite the shipping and weaving of various items. Now, the shop has received more than 100 boxes of new summer clothing materials in the past two days, which is just enough to meet the demand. In order to consistently adhere to the business policy of "profiting from volume," the shop will continue to sell all items at low prices. This is truly good news for ladies from all walks of life who want to make new summer clothes.

Theater News

The Baixing Grand Theater at the intersection of Laobazi Road and Fusheng Road declares that it will be screening the only silent adventurous romance, the latest masterpiece, starting today.

The New Central Theater declares: Movie star Zhang Zhiyun is famous at home and abroad for her two films, "Empty Valley Orchid" and "Plum Blossom Falling." In other words, these two films are Zhang Zhiyun's launching works. Since Zhang left the screen, these two films have become more famous, especially "Plum Blossom Falling," which is the most popular. Moreover, this film has not been re-screened in theaters north of Shanghai for a long time. In order to give preferential treatment to the audience, this theater has specially requested the Mingxing Company to rent and screen it for three days, and has lowered the ticket price for evening shows by 10 cents, the same as the daytime show price. The theater is also fully equipped with electric fans, so even in the hot summer, you will not feel the heat.

Medical News

Bao Ru Hospital declares: German female doctor Jiang Bao Ru has many years of clinical experience and has served as a doctor in major hospitals in this city and other cities. Now she has established this hospital at No. 108 Xizilaihuo Street, the intersection of French Concession Ma Road. It is divided into internal medicine, obstetrics, gynecology, pediatrics, dermatology, venereology, and various injections for leucorrhea and spermatorrhea. The fees are very low. The grand opening will be held today, with free consultations for three days, with only a 20-cent registration fee. Free consultations will also be provided every afternoon to benefit the poor and sick.

Shifang Hospital on Er Ma Road declares: This hospital was founded by the famous doctor Tu Qihua. For more than ten years, it has enjoyed a remarkable reputation and treats various internal and external departments. It is especially well-known for venereology. Recently, Mr. Sun, a member of the banking industry, suffered from gout, with alternating chills and fever, and was unable to move an inch. After several diagnoses and treatments, none were effective. Later, introduced by a friend, Dr. Tu personally examined him and diagnosed it as gonorrheal arthritis. Using the latest scientific methods of acupuncture and medicine, he was completely cured in less than a week.

The office of traditional Chinese medicine doctor Xu Bingxiong declares: This doctor is a third-generation family doctor. He has a clinic in a residential house on Dou Market Street (Xu Lu), specializing in various internal medicine diseases, especially skilled in the diagnosis and treatment of pulmonary tuberculosis. With more than 50 years of research experience, he carefully studies medical theories. Every consultation is effective. If you ask for treatment, he is humble and willing to discuss in detail, without the habits of famous doctors, and does not limit the time. Even if you go in the morning and leave in the evening (if he is not out on a house call), he is always available for consultation. Therefore, people from all walks of life trust and seek treatment from him, regardless of medical fees or poverty. In addition to providing medical treatment, he also gives away medicine from the Lao Lai Yi Pharmacy to benefit poor and suffering people. There are many disciples serving him, and Chen Chuyuan and others are the most prominent, with a thorough understanding of medical theories. Currently, due to other business relationships, they are still secretly reluctant to come forward.
